<b>matampúhun</b> <i>a</i> @generous in contributing.

<b>tampuk_{1}</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [AB2456; ac] stab so as to
make the instrument stick, be sticking in.
<i>Akuy mitampuk ug lápis sa báni,</i> I stuck
a pencil into the banana trunk. <i>Báraw nga
mitampuk sa dughan,</i> A knife sticking into
the breast. <b>2</b> [A; a] beat s.t. with the inside
of the fist (as if sticking a dagger into it).
<i>Mitagubtub ang ákung likud nga íyang gitampuk,</i>
My back resounded when he hit it
with his fist. <b>-in-an</b> <i>a</i> jewelry having precious
stones embedded. [+]

<b>tampuk_{2}</b> <i>v</i> [A; c1] gather and @dump into
s.t. <i>Ang mutsatsa mauy nagtampuk sa mga
bulingun sa planggána,</i> The maid put the
dirty laundry into the basin. <i>Tampúkun
(itampuk) ku ang mga basíyung láta sa dakung
kahun,</i> I will dump the empty cans
into the big box.

<b>tampulung</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B56] @loom, @{stand out} large.
<i>Dúnay dakung batu nga nagtampulung daplin
sa likuánan sa dálan,</i> There is a huge
rock looming at the side of the road at the
bend. <b>2</b> [A; b6c1] pile or heap stones. <i>Magtampulung
siyag mga batu líbut sa ílang balay,</i>
He will pile stones around their house
as a wall. <i>n</i> <b>1</b> large rock or pile of stones
that stands prominently in the middle of the
sea, protruding or immersed under shallow
water. <b>2</b> a dike of piled stones in the sea,
constructed to trap fish behind it when the
tide goes out.

<b>tampúng</b> = <sc>TAMPULUNG</sc>.

<b>tampuug</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A3] @loom large, @{stand out}
prominently. <i>Nagtampuug sa dálan ang buldúsir,</i>
The bulldozer is looming large on the
road. <b>2</b> [B6; c1P] be piled in a large heap.
<i>Nagtampuug ang sagbut sa búngun sa ílang
balay,</i> There is a huge @pile of garbage beneath
their house. <i>Ngánung gipatampuug
(gitampuug) nímu ang makinilyahúnun únà
mu buháta?</i> Why did you allow the typing
to @{pile up} before working on it?

<i>Ug magkupya ka, tamda sígi ang pahina,</i>

ang ági,</i> Don't trace on top of the book because

ang dápit sa sugilánun kay ákung gitamdan

<b>4c</b> [b(1)] @remember, make a @note of.<i> Tamdi

by bit. <b>(<-)</b> <i>v</i> [A2C; c1] @group or @join together.

<b>timuri</b> <i>n</i> a k.o. secret talk where certain phonemes
are substituted for others: <i>u</i> for <i>a</i>, <i>t</i>
for <i>d</i>, <i>p</i> for <i>d</i>, <i>r</i> for <i>l</i>, <i>n</i> for <i>m</i>, and <i>y</i> for <i>s</i>,
the rest remaining. The word <i>timuri</i> is derived
from <i>binali</i> ('done backwards'). <i>v</i> [A;
a2] speak in <i>timuri</i>. <i>Kumuu kung nutimuri?
(Kamau kang mubinali?)</i> Cangre yougre
speakgre Hoggre? (Can you speak Hog Latin?)

<b>ting-</b> prefix added to roots which refer to s.t.
which happens seasonally to form nouns
which mean 'season or time of the day that
[so-and-so] takes place'. Most forms with
<i>ting-</i> have short penults. <i>Sayung buntag nga
mauy tinglusad sa manuk,</i> The early morning
hours when the chickens come down
from their perches. <i>Tingbunga (tingpamunga)
sa mangga,</i> The mango season. <i>Tingadlaw
(ting-adlaw),</i> The hot season. <i>Tingbálud,</i>
The wavy season.

teeth. <b>2</b> k.o. reddish breast tumor believed
to be caused by eating any k.o. shellfish
with nipple-like growths, and treated with
steam from those k.o. shellfish. <i>v</i> [A123P]
<b>1</b> have food particles lodged in the teeth.
<i>Makatinga (makapatinga) ang karni sa ngípun,</i>
Meat sticks in the teeth. <b>2</b> get this k.o.
tumor.

payment. <i>n</i> partial payment given in
advance.

<b>tingála</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B1256; b3(1)c5] be @surprised,
@mystified at s.t. unexpected. <i>Natingála ku

<sc>TINGÁLA</sc>, <i>2</i>. <b>2</b> be ill at ease from being new

inches taller. <i>Gitubúan na ang sinínà,</i> She
has @outgrown her dress. <i>Ang gitubúan sa
dákit,</i> Where the banyan tree was @growing.
<b>2</b> @{earn interest}. <i>Mutúbù ang kwartang ibangku,</i>

[b(1)] @{develop feelings}. <i>Gitubúan kug kasína
sa íyang paglampus,</i> I grew envious over
his success. <b>4</b> [A2S] for water, dough, land

anak nga utukan,</i> They are mostly imbeciles,

<i>n</i> <b>1</b> time used for make-up. <i>Ang trabáhu run
tupus sa pista upisiyal gahápun,</i> Today's
work is to make up for yesterday's holiday.
<b>2</b> s.t. just as much so in exactly the opposite
way. <i>Dátù mi niadtu, tupus pud run nga
kakha tukà,</i> We used to be just as rich as we
are poor now. <i>Pagkagarbúsang bayhána, tupus
sa íyang bánang labihan kamapaubsánun,</i>

is modest.

<b>u_{1}</b> @or. <i>Kinsa may muadtu, ikaw u aku?</i> Who
will go, you or me? <i>Muadtu ka ba u pabilin
ba,</i> Are you going or staying here? <b>-- byín</b>,
<b>bín</b> <i>particle offering two choices of action:</i>
or, if you wish. <i>Ikaw bay muanhi u byin[**byín] aku
bay muanhà?</i> Are you coming here, or
shall I go there?

<b>u_{2}</b> <b>1</b> <i>particle initial in the sentence:</i> exclamation
of surprise upon finding out s.t. <b>1a</b> expressing
annoyed surprise. <i>U, ngánung kúlang
man ning suklì!</i> Hey, this isn't enough
change! <i>U, ngánung mipaúlì ka pa man!</i>
What are you doing back here! <i>U, ngánung
wà man siya mukúyug!</i> Why? How come
she's not with you? <i>U, mudílì ka na hinúun
nga náa gitúnul na?</i> You mean you are going
to refuse it when you already have it in
your hand? <b>1b</b> expressing pleasant surprise.
<i>U, Ting! Nía man diay ka!</i> Hey, Ting.
You're here! <b>1c</b> exclaiming surprise at having
made a mistake: Oh! <i>U, singku písus
ba diay tu ímung gihátag nákù?</i> Oh! Was
it five pesos you gave me? <b>2</b> exclamation
preceding an emphatic denial. <i>U dílì, dílì nà
mahímù,</i> Oh no, that can't be done. <b>2a</b> preceding
a statement that s.t. is not the way
the interlocutor thought. <i>U, sayun ra nang</i>
-----File: 2187.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>lutúun. Lat-i lang,</i> Oh, that's easy to cook.
Just boil it. <b>3</b> pause before speaking. <i>U, ári
diri nà ibutang,</i> Oh, just put that over here.
<b>4</b> (most often at the end of the clause) particle
to draw s.o.'s attention. <i>U, Dyú, dalì
ra kadiyut,</i> Oh, Joe[**,?] would you come here
a second. <i>Ambi ra nang lápis u,</i> Would you
hand me that pencil, that one over there.
<i>Díay písus u. Patupi didtu,</i> Here, here's a
peso. Go get a haircut.

<b>ug</b> <i>short form:</i> <b>g.</b> particle showing grammatical
relation between two forms. <b>1</b> preceding
non-specific goals. <i>Mipalit siya ug libru,</i> He
bought a book. <i>Gitagáan ku níyag kindi</i>, He
gave me some candy. <b>1a</b> preceding a noun
referring to s.t. specific, but referring to it
as s.t. general on any and all occasions. <i>Dì
síya muadtug Manílà,</i> He refuses to go to
any[**? P2] Manila. <b>1b</b> <b>ása --</b> where is one to get.
<i>Ása man ka ug kwartang ibáyad ánà?</i> Where
will you get the money to pay for that? <b>2</b>
preceding infinitives (replacing a prefix
<i>pag-</i>).<i> Naglísud ku ug saka,</i> I had a hard time
going up. <b>2a</b> with adjectives of manner. <i>Milakaw
siya ug kusug,</i> He walked away fast.
<b>2a1</b> <b>-- ímu</b>, <b>íya</b>, <b>íla</b>, <b>etc.</b>[**?] by yourself, himself,
themselves, etc. <i>Káun ug ímu,</i> Just go ahead
and eat on your own. <i>Mutúyuk ug íya ra,</i>
It will turn all by itself. <b>2b</b> after <i>ayaw</i>. <i>Ayaw
siya ug tan-áwa,</i> Don't look at him. <b>3</b> <i>adj.</i>
plus <b>ug</b> <i>plus noun:</i> 'have'. <i>Si Pidru dakù ug
buktun,</i> Pedro has big arms. <i>Uy, kanindut
bayà níya ug mata!</i> What beautiful eyes
she has! <b>4</b> preceding a non-specific genitive.
<b>4a</b> marking the possessor. <i>Anak ug hárì,</i>
The son of a king. <b>4b</b> marking the agent.
<i>Gidágit ug banug,</i> Was taken by a hawk. <b>5</b>
if, when. <i>Ug maabut siya, pahibaw-a ku,</i>
When he arrives, notify me. <i>Ug aku pa nímu,</i>
If I were you. <b>5a</b> <i>with indirect questions:</i>
whether. <i>Pangutan-a siya ug muabut
ba ang barku ugmà,</i> Ask him whether the
boat will arrive tomorrow. <b>5a1</b> with indirect
questions containing interrogatives. <i>Nangutána
aku ug unsa nà,</i> I asked what that was.
<b>5b</b> linker for qualifying phrases. <i>Nákù ug
ímu nang nahuman,</i> I thought you had finished
it already. <i>Tingáli ug muanhi siya
ugmà,</i> Perhaps he will come tomorrow. <i>Syáru
ug dì nà mahímù,</i> I don't believe that is
impossible. <b>6</b> @or. <i>Pritúhun ug tuláhun, paríha
ra nákù,</i> Deep fried or stewed, it's all
the same to me. <b>7</b> @{and}. <i>Lakaw ug ayaw pagbálik!</i>
Go away, and don't come back! <i>Si-</i>*
-----File: 2197.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>*la si Huwan ug si Pidru ang mianhi,</i> John
and Pedro were the ones who came here.

<b>ugdul</b> <i>a</i> @short, @trimmed. <i>Gipalabihag ugdul
níya ang íyang buhuk,</i> She had her hair cut
very short. <i>v</i> [B12; c1] be @trimmed short.
<i>Naugdul ang mga mais kay giharíag tuhak
sa manuk,</i> The chickens pecked the corn
plants right down.

<b>ugdung</b> = <sc>UGDU_{1}</sc>.

<b>ughad</b> <i>a</i> for a throat to be sore. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [B; b6]
for the throat to get sore. <i>Nag-ughad ang ákung
tunlan. Ubhun tingáli ku,</i> I have a sore
throat. I'm probably getting a cough. <b>2</b> [AN;
c1] expel phlegm by coughing it out
hard.

<b>ughak</b> = <sc>UDHAK</sc>.

<b>ugíngut</b> <i>n</i> @{body odor} of unwashed perspiration
and dirt. <i>Nanimáhù lang kang ugíngut,</i>
You have a terrible <sc>B.O.</sc>

<b>ugis</b> a <b>1</b> having completely white feathers.
<i>Limpiyu tan-áwun ang ugis nga manuk,</i>
White-feathered chickens look clean. <b>2</b> @fair
of complexion. <i>Ugis kaáyu sila,</i> They are
very @white. <b>2a</b> people belonging to the white
race. <b>2b</b> @albino. <i>v</i> [B26; b6] be, become
@white-feathered, @white-skinned.

<b>ugíut</b> = <sc>ÍGUT_{1}</sc>.

<b>ugkad</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; a] dig, @{pull out} s.t. that is
completely or partly buried or contained
inside s.t. else. <i>Láing dyíp ang miugkad sa
dyíp nga nalubung sa lápuk,</i> Another jeep
pulled out the jeep that got stuck in the
mud. <i>Ang nakaugkad sa buláwang budha,</i>
The man who @{dug up} the golden Buddha.
<i>Giugkad sa kawatan ang ákung kaban,</i> The
thief dug up the things in my trunk. <b>2</b> [A12;
b8] find s.t. that was in s.t. or buried.

<b>ugkal</b> = <sc>UKAL</sc>.

<b>ugkat</b> <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; a1b2] dig s.t. out from under
s.t. <i>Giugkat níla ang natabunan,</i> They dug
out the person who had been buried. <b>2</b> [A;
a12] @{dig out} or @{find out} s.t. not known.
<i>Buut ba ninyung ugkátun ang ákung kagahápun?</i>
Do you want to @{dig into} my past?

<b>ugkay</b> (from <i>ukay</i>) <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A; ab2] @{dig out} s.t.
buried. <i>Mga pulis ang nag-ugkay sa gilubngan
sa gibunù,</i> The policemen @exhumed
the murder victim. <b>1a</b> [A; a12] @ransack
things in looking for s.t. <i>Ákung ugkáyun
ang mga butang nímu básug túa didtu ang
ákung rilu,</i> I'll ransack your things in case
